<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>Recently, ultra-high frequency (UHF) near-field radio frequency identification (RFID) technology has gained much attention due to its applications in item-level RFID applications, such as pharmaceutical and retailing industry. The RFID systems based on near-field communications need a special reader antenna that can generate strong and uniform magnetic field in its interrogation zone. UHF near-field reader antennas play an essential role in UHF near-field RFID systems. It directly affects the reading distance and reading rate.</p><p>Solid-line loops have been used as reader antennas in low-frequency (LF) and high-frequency (HF) RFID systems. This type of antenna is electrically small. However, it is no longer electrically small in UHF near-field RFID systems in order to offer a larger interrogation zone. When it is electrically large or comparable to one wavelength, the current distribution along the loop reverses at every half-wavelength. In this case, the magnetic near field of the antenna is weak and nonuniform. For these reasons, the solid-line loop with stub phase shifter together with segmented loop structures <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>â<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a> are widely used in UHF near-field RFID antennas to obtain in-phase current distribution. The stub phase shifter enlarges the size but not the interrogation zone of the antenna. Currently, dual-printed dipoles <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a> or left-handed loading techniques <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a> are used to improve the performance of the loop antennas. Although the currents along the loops can be kept in-phase, the interrogation zone of the reader is still small. A planar antenna using two coupled patches with a microstrip line feed <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a> has a large interrogation zone, but the magnetic field of the antenna is nonuniform. In <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>, a robust UHF near-field reader antenna using a coplanar stripline is proposed to deliver uniform magnetic near field. However, the lumped balun in the antenna will cause power consumption and reading distance decline.</p><p>In this letter, a novel reader antenna based on double-sided parallel-strip line (DSPSL) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_1">[9]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_1">[10]</a> is proposed for UHF near-field RFID systems. Both the simulation and measurement results show that the antenna exhibits strong and uniform vertical magnetic field distribution in a large interrogation zone. The fabricated antenna works from 887 to 938 MHz with reflection coefficient less than â10 dB. The measured maximum reading distance is greater than 200 mm with 30 dBm input power. When the input power is dropped to 17 dBm, the maximum reading distance is still greater than 70 mm, and 100% reading rate is achieved within a distance of 5 mm. In addition, with 10 dBm input power, the reading rate is still greater than 80% on the surface of the proposed antenna.</p></div>

The antenna is composed of a phase inverter, DSPSL structures, and four dipoles. The inner area of the dipole loop is the designed interrogation zone. Since the arm length of each dipole is less than half of the wavelength, the current along the dipole loop is kept in the same direction. It produces strong and uniform magnetic field in the region inside the dipole loop. <p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 2</a> shows the simulated current distribution of the proposed antenna. It is clear that the currents of the proposed antenna are in-phase along four dipoles. Such current distribution results in uniform magnetic field distribution over the interrogation zone.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 2. </b><fig>Simulated current distribution of the proposed antenna at 920 MHz.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6747985/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>

<p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 5</a> shows the simulated reflection coefficient of the proposed antenna for different values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-45-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-355" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-356"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-357"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-358" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-359"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-360"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-361" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">7</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-45">L_{7}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It can be seen that as <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-46-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-362" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-363"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-364"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-365" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-366"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-367"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-368" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">7</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-46">L_{7}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases from 5 to 10 mm, the reflection coefficient gets smaller. However, the reflection coefficient deteriorates to â12 dBm when the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-47-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-369" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-370"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-371"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-372" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-373"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-374"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-375" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">7</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-47">L_{7}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> increases from 10 to 40 mm. It means that the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-48-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-376" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-377"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-378"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-379" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-380"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-381"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-382" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">7</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-48">L_{7}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> can neither be too big nor too small to achieve good impedance matching. The similar phenomenon can be observed in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 6</a>. The reason is that the impedance of the offset DSPSL is changed as changing the values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-49-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-383" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-384"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-385"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-386" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-387"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-388"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-389" style="font-size: 70.7%; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-49">L_{7}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-50-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-390" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-391"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-392"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; It also leads to the impedance change of the antenna. By selecting appropriate values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-51-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-397" role="math" style="width: 1.565em; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.964em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-401"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-402"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-403" style="font-size: 70.7%; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-412"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-413"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-53">L_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>. It is observed that when changing the value of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-54-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-418" role="math" style="width: 1.204em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1001.08em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-419"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-420"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.084em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-421" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">L</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-422"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-423"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-424" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">5</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-54">L_{5}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from 65 to 67 mm, the operating frequency of the antenna is shifted downward.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 7. </b><fig>Simulated reflection coefficient of the proposed antenna for different values of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-55-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-425" role="math" style="width: 1.458em; <p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Measurements and Results</h2></div><p>The proposed antenna was fabricated and measured with the same dimensions as the simulated ones. The reflection coefficient of the fabricated antenna was measured using Agilent E5071C network analyzer as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 8</a>. The measured impedance bandwidth of the proposed antenna for <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-56-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-432" role="math" style="width: 5.949em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 5.348em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1005.11em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-433"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-434" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-435"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.384em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-436"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-437"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-438" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-439"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-440"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-441" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">11</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-442" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">|</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-443" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">&lt;</span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-444" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">â</span><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-445" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">10</span><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-446" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Â </span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-56">\vert{S}_{11}\vert&lt;-10~</script></tex-math></inline-formula> dB is 51 MHz (from 887 to 938 MHz). The measured result agrees very well with the simulation result.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 8. </b><fig>Simulated and measured reflection coefficient of the proposed antenna.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6747985/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 9. </b><fig>Photograph of the proposed antenna and its measurement setup.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6747985/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p>To further verify the performance of the proposed antenna, extensive experiments have been performed by using the professional tag and reader. The measurement configuration is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 9</a>. The antenna prototype was connected to the Impinj Speedway Revolution reader R220 to detect the Impinj button type tag (J41, 11 mm in diameter).</p><p>The surface of the antenna was marked by 1Ã1-cm<sup>2</sup> grids. The tag was positioned on the slider of a foam ruler. We recorded the reading distances at all the grids by moving the foam ruler and the tag across the surface of the antenna.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig.Â 10</a> presents the measured reading area and the simulated vertical magnetic field distribution of the proposed antenna at the heights of 3, 8, and 13 cm, respectively. The input power in measurement is 30 dBm. The wire frames represent the metal part of the antenna. The black sections shown in the first row of the figure represent the measured readable area. The color ones shown in the second row of the figure are the simulated readable area. Only a small difference is observed between the measured reading range and simulated one.

top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-516"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-517"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-519"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-520"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-521" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">r</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-522" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-61">S_{\rm rz}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the area of the readable zone inside the interrogation zone, and <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-62-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-523" role="math" style="width: 1.324em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.264em 1001.2em 2.465em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-524"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-525"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.204em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1000.66em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-526" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-527"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-528"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-529" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">i</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-530" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">z</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.197em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-62">S_{\rm iz}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the area of the interrogation zone. In general, when the input power is changed from 30 to 10 dBm, the reading rate as well as the maximum reading distance declined. However, the maximum reading distance of the reader with the proposed antenna is greater than 200 mm when there is 30 dBm input power. When the input power is 17 dBm, the maximum reading distance is still greater than 70 mm, and 100% reading rate is achieved within a distance of 5 mm. In addition, with 10 dBm input power, the reading rate is still greater than 80% on the surface of the proposed antenna.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig.Â 11. </b><fig>Measured reading rate of the proposed antenna at different distances with different input power.</fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/6747985/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<p></p><p><a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">TableÂ I</a> compares the measured maximum reading distance of the proposed antenna to those using other techniques. Although the different readers and tags will affect the reading distances, it still illustrates that reading distance of the proposed antenna is quite good.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">TABLEÂ I </b>Measured Maximum Reading Distance Comparison Among Near-Field UHF RFID Reader Antennas<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/7727/6719497/6747985/6747985-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table " /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div>
<p></p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Conclusion</h2></div><p>A novel UHF near-field RFID reader antenna has been proposed in this letter. The fabricated antenna works from 887 to 938 MHz with reflection coefficient less than â10 dB. The use of the phase inverter and the four dipoles in the proposed antenna lead to strong and uniform magnetic near field, which enables long reading distance for the near-field RFID system with the antenna. Measurements show that the maximum reading distances are 200 and 70 mm with 30 and 17 dBm input power, respectively. The antenna can work with very low input power as well as much higher power in near-field tag detecting.</p></div>
</div></div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>
